ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="palliative-care">PALLIATIVE CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palliative-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It's an approach that improves the quality of life of patients and their families facing problems associated with life threatening illness, through prevention and relief of surgery the early impeccable assessment and treatment of pain and other problems: physical, psychosocial and spiritual (WHO) 2002.</li>
<li>List the conditions or diseases for palliative care</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-palliative">PRINCIPLES OF PALLIATIVE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-palliative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Provides relief from pain and other different symptoms</li>
<li>Affirm life and regards dying as a normal process</li>
<li>Intends neither to hasten nor postpone death</li>
<li>Intergrates the psychological and spiritual aspects of patient care</li>
<li>Offers a support system to help patients live as actively as possible until death</li>
<li>Offers a support system to help the family cope during the patients illness and in their own bereavement</li>
<li>Uses a team approach to address the needs of patients and their families including bereavement counseling if indicated</li>
<li>Will enhance quality of life and also positively influence the care of illness.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-a442c6e9.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="history-of-pallitive-care">HISTORY OF PALLITIVE CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-of-pallitive-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In late 1950's Dr Cicely Sainder played a role in establishing the modern science and art of caring for patients with life threatening diseases illnesses and founded the first modern hospice at St Christopher's in southern London that started in 1967</li>
<li>The first PC service in Africa was island hospice in Zimbabwe which operated in 1979 followed by South Africa, Kenya and Uganda.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fundamentals-of-palliative-care">FUNDAMENTALS OF PALLIATIVE CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fundamentals-of-palliative-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The following concepts are applicable for effective delivery of palliative care</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Holistic care
This approach regards the patient as a whole person, recognizing them as comprising of physiological, social and physical aspects and is culturally appropriate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patient centered care
PC advocates that patient should be the center of care, focus around patient wishes. This aspect respects the patients decision on their care and treatment options</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teamwork and partnership
No single profession can adequately address all issues arising from a life limiting diagnosis. Constant exposure to patients distressing circumstances can be emotionally draining on staff and care givers. This calls for interdisciplinary approach for effective PC</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fundamentals-cont">FUNDAMENTALS (CONT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fundamentals-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-family-and-community">4. Family and community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-family-and-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Care for patients with life limiting conditions will take place in range of a community based settings. These includes patients home palliative care units or residential care facilities, Referral pathways and linkages between community based PC, hospitals based and hospices plays a big role.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-ethical-legal-aspect">MEDICAL ETHICAL-LEGAL ASPECT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-ethical-legal-aspect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-autonomy">1. Autonomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-autonomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This means self-rule. Respect for autonomy promotes the individuals right to make his/her own decision</li>
<li>Information sharing is based on a good communication understanding including how much the patients wants to know</li>
<li>Respect for autonomy includes addressing concepts such as informed consent, confidentiality and truth telling</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-beneficence-and-non-maleficence">2. Beneficence and non-maleficence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-beneficence-and-non-maleficence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Beneficence (benefit to the patient) and non-maleficence (to do no harm). In medical treatment, any intervention also carry a risk of harm e.g side effects, radiotherapy. These must be weighed against the offer of cure or disease control and reflect on patients cure decision.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Justice</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In these case competing claims are decided in fairness. It can be considered according to distributive justice (fair distribution of resources) right based- all have right to health care and legal justice according to the countrys laws</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>NB. Write short notes on issues pertaining - Patients rights, will writing, euthanasia.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="distressing-symptoms-in-palliative-care">DISTRESSING SYMPTOMS IN PALLIATIVE CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#distressing-symptoms-in-palliative-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Patients with life threatening illnesses experiences various distressing symptoms that effect their quality of life</li>
<li>Common symptoms in palliative care</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Anorexia and cachexia.</li>
<li>pain</li>
<li>Breathlessness</li>
<li>Confusion</li>
<li>Constipation</li>
<li>Dehydration</li>
<li>Diarrhea</li>
<li>Distress</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Malnutrition</li>
<li>Nausea and vomiting</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anorexia-and-cachexia-malnutrition">ANOREXIA AND CACHEXIA/ MALNUTRITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anorexia-and-cachexia-malnutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Weakness, profound weight loss and poor appetite are common problems in advanced cancer, HIV and AIDS and end stage organ failure</li>
<li>Cachexia is not associated with hunger or thirst nor will it improve by forced feeding and hydration</li>
<li>Anorexia and malnutrition could be due to reversible causes e.g. lack of available or digestible foods, dysphagia, sore mouth, altered taste, nausea vomiting, constipation pain and metabolic disturbances (hypocalcaemia or uremia)</li>
<li>Anorexia could also be secondary to treatment e.g. chemotherapy, radiotherapy or drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<ul>
<li>Management</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Support family and patient</li>
<li>Identify the cause and manage using pharmacological and non-pharmacological</li>
<li>Support family and patient</li>
<li>Serve small appetizing meals and emphasize on fluid intake.</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="breathlessness">BREATHLESSNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breathlessness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is a subjective experience of breathing discomfort</li>
<li>Difficult in breathing is a frightening experience, patients describe it as suffocating, could not get enough air, chocking, felt like I was about to die.</li>
<li>Causes</li>
<li>Respiratory:- primary or secondary lung cancer, pulmonary embolus, airway tumor, infection</li>
<li>Cardiac :- superior vena cava obstruction, anaemia, cardiac failure, pericardial effusion.</li>
<li>others include - Ascitis, pneumonectomy</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Management</strong></li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Take holistic history-severity duration</li>
<li>Treat reversible condition e.g anemia, infection</li>
<li>Address underlying anxiety</li>
<li>Use medication to relieve symptoms e.g morphine 2-2.5mg 4hrly, diazepine 2-5 mg for anxiety and panic, dexamethasone 8-12 mg daily for causes like superior vena cava obstruction, lymphangitis</li>
<li>Consider other medication e.g bronchodilators, diuretics.</li>
<li>Other supportive measures e.g aeration positioning fluid management</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="confusion">CONFUSION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#confusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>One of the distressing and difficult to manage symptom</li>
<li>Causes  may include; uncontrolled pain, urinary retention, severe constipation, hypoxia, metabolic disturbance, systemic infections etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>use pharmacological and non-pharmacological interventions</li>
<li>Keep surrounding calm and familiar, orientate patient on time and place.</li>
<li>Avoid restraining unless for patient safety</li>
<li>Support the families to be able to stay with patient</li>
<li>Give haloperidol (0.5-5mg) tds and benzodiazepine e.g diazepam 5-10 mg</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="constipation">CONSTIPATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#constipation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the passage of small, hard fecal materials infrequently and with difficult causes</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>direct effect of disease (internal obstruction from tumor in the bowel</li>
<li>External compression from abdominal muscles</li>
<li>Low fiber in the diet</li>
<li>Decreased food intake</li>
<li>Dehydration</li>
<li>General body weakness</li>
<li>Damage to lumber-sacral spinal cord</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Encourage fluid and fruit intake, vegetables and fibre</li>
<li>Encourage mobility and proper positioning</li>
<li>Give relaxatives with opioids e.g bisacodyl 5mg</li>
<li>Assess obstruction</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pain">PAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Definition</li>
<li>Is an unpleasant sensory and emotional experience associated with actual or potential tissue damage.</li>
<li>It is subjective and what the patient describes as hurts.</li>
<li>Is a common symptom among patients with life threatening diseases.</li>
<li>Over 80% of patients with cancer and 50% patients with PLWHIV have moderate to severe pain.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pain-cont">PAIN (cont)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pain-cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-pain">TYPES OF PAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

i. nociceptive and neuropathic
ii. acute and chronic</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-pain">ACUTE PAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Acute pain is related to an easily identified pathophysiology</li>
<li>Resolution is within days or weeks</li>
<li>Chronic pain is not related to an easily identified condition</li>
<li>May be present for a prolonged period of time</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nociceptive-pain">NOCICEPTIVE PAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nociceptive-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Involves direct stimulation of intact mechanical chemical and thermal nociceptors, transmitted along functional nerves.</li>
<li>Divided into: - a) somatic pain (skin, systematic tissue, muscles an bone)  is due to a stimulation of the somatic nervous system  pain is described as aching or throbbing, easily localised</li>
<li>b) Visceral pain- (cardiac, lung, GIT tract)  involves stimulation of autonomic nervous system</li>
<li>Pain difficult to describe or localise</li>
<li>Nociceptives responds to opioids and or co-analgesics.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY OHSAS 18001:2015</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neuropathic-pain">NEUROPATHIC PAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neuropathic-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Results from disordered function of the peripheral or central nervous system due to any of the many potentials</li>
<li>Pain is described as burning, tingling, numbness, shooting, stabbing, or electric  feeling may respond to opioid analgesics, but adjuvant analgesics (tricyclic antidepressant, anticonvulsants) are often required in combination with opioids to achieve adequate relief.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>

<ol>
<li>THE GOLDEN RULE</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="end-of-life-care">END OF LIFE CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#end-of-life-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Definition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>End of life; this refers to the final phase of a patient's illness when death is impending</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>END OF LIFE CARE</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is the term used for issues related to death and dying and service addressed to these issues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>End of life care (EOC) focuses on physical and psychosocial needs for the patient and the family</p>
</li>
</ul>

Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY OMS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-management">PRINCIPLES OF MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Have good symptoms control</li>
<li>Review all drugs and symptoms</li>
<li>Avoid unnecessary intervention</li>
<li>Maintain effective communication</li>
<li>Ensure care for the family</li>
<li>Assess and refer early to specialists service for patient and family support if needed.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY OMS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-symptoms-of-end-life">COMMON SYMPTOMS OF END LIFE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-symptoms-of-end-life" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Decreased socialization and withdrawal</li>
<li>Terminal breathlessness</li>
<li>Nausea and vomiting</li>
<li>Decreased food and fluid intake</li>
<li>Loss of bladder and bowel control</li>
<li>Skin cold especially the limbs</li>
<li>Death rattle</li>
<li>Delirium.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-during-the-end-of-life-care">MANAGEMENT DURING THE END OF LIFE CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-the-end-of-life-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environment">ENVIRONMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Patient to be in a quiet private room and well ventilated and well lit.</li>
<li>Limit visitation 2 at a time</li>
<li>Prescence of a loved one holding hands, touching or praying brings comfort to the patient</li>
<li>Involve the patient in discussion at the side bed even if he appears unconscious or asleep.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychological-care">PSYCHOLOGICAL CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychological-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Recognize and address the physical and emotional issues facing the patients family</li>
<li>Identify the family or other people involved and keep them informed</li>
<li>Be honest</li>
<li>Listen and explain what is likely to happen</li>
<li>Be available</li>
<li>Reassure them that symptom control will continue</li>
<li>Encourage family to do small tasks for the loved one</li>
<li>Communicate with their loved one to remain close</li>
<li>Touch, smile and understand the patients feelings</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Address religious concern  terminally ill patients receive a lot of comfort and relief from their faith</li>
<li>Some patients will ask for their spiritual leaders to get spiritual guidance</li>
<li>Non-Christians will need to be baptized to meet their impending death</li>
<li>Nurse to talk tactfully to those who do not ask for their spiritual leader.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-needs">PHYSICAL NEEDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-needs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Swallowing and coughing reflexes will be affected, expectorants accumulate in the mouth and throat  patients may aspirate</li>
<li>Position patients on his side  for secretions to flow</li>
<li>Suction should be done</li>
<li>Nutritional and fluid input is reduced  lips may crack</li>
<li>Keep the mouth clean and moist  lubricate the mouth and the lips with paraffin</li>
<li>Nose kept clear and lubricated..</li>
<li>Eyes wiped with cotton wool to remove secretion using normal saline.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED MANAGEMENT SYSTEM</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrition">NUTRITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Normally patient has very little interest in foods and fluids - no appetite and no physical effort to eat and drink.</li>
<li>Meet nutritional needs effectively by administration of intravenous fluids or nasogastric tube feeding  too much may cause abdominal disturbance as gastric activities are reduced</li>
<li>If swallowing reflex is intact, you can give sips of water frequently chips of ice or just moistening the lips with a dump cloth.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="elimination-need">ELIMINATION NEED<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elimination-need" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If patient is incontinence change the linen, use pampers and catheterize also do pressure areas.</li>
<li>If there is difficult in elimination, then enema may be given constant catheterization.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>

<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dysnoea">dysnoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dysnoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="death-process">DEATH PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#death-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Caring for a person during the last few weeks and days of life can be stressful and demanding. Many different feelings and emotions may surface at this time.</li>
<li>Carers are often concerned that death will be a painful experience for the person. However, the time before death is generally peaceful. There is a gentle winding down that may take several days. The body starts to let go of life. If restlessness does occur, it can be treated.</li>
<li>Not all the signs discussed below will occur with every person, nor will they occur in any particular sequence. Sometimes these signs appear a few hours before death, sometimes a few days. These physical signs are part of the normal, natural process of the persons body gradually slowing down.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY</p>
<ul>
<li>Apart from the signs described here, one may notice other signs.</li>
<li>One can bring enormous benefit to the person one is caring for simply by sitting with them, holding their hand and speaking in a calm and reassuring manner. Even when the person does not respond, they can probably hear you. Being with can be more important than doing for.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY OMS-3</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="changes-expected">CHANGES EXPECTED<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#changes-expected" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="appetite-and-thirst">APPETITE AND THIRST<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#appetite-and-thirst" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The persons appetite and thirst may decrease, and they may have little desire to eat or drink. This concerns many carers, but is a natural process and is not painful for the person.</p>
<p>Sips of water, or a moist mouth swab will help them.</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sleep-and-alertness">SLEEP AND ALERTNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sleep-and-alertness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Changes happening in the persons body mean that they may spend a lot of time asleep, may be drowsy and difficult to wake up.</li>
<li>Talk to the person when they seem most alert, and allow them to sleep when they want to. There is no need to shake the person or to speak loudly. It is best to speak softly and naturally.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY OMS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="temperature">TEMPERATURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#temperature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The bodys temperature may change. At one time the persons hands, feet and legs may be increasingly cool to the touch, and at others they may be hot and clammy. Sometimes parts of the persons body become blotchy and darker in colour. This is due to the circulation of the blood slowing down and is a normal part of the dying process.</li>
<li>If the person indicates that they feel cold, use light bedding to keep them warm. Provide good ventilation; a fan to circulate the air and cool damp towels can help if the person seems hot.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="secretions">SECRETIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secretions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>As coughing and swallowing reflexes slow down, saliva and mucus may collect in the back of the persons throat, causing a gurgling, bubbling or other noise.</li>
<li>This noise does not usually cause distress to the person. To help improve the situation you can lift the persons head and support them with pillows so that their head is turned to one side.</li>
<li>Medications can also be given to slow down the production of saliva and mucus and thus improve comfort.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY OMS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="incontinence">INCONTINENCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incontinence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The amount of urine that the body is producing decreases due to the reduced amount of fluid the person is drinking. The urine may become stronger and darker in color. The person may lose control of their bladder and bowels.</li>
<li>This does not happen to all people, but if it does there are pads, and special absorbent sheets to enhance comfort and hygiene.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="breathing">BREATHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Regular breathing patterns may change. Sometimes the breathing may be fast, and at other times there may be long gaps between breaths. Breathing may be shallow or noisy. This, too, is due to blood circulation slowing down and a build up in the bodys waste products. It is not painful or distressing for the person.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="restlessness">RESTLESSNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restlessness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Due to the decrease in circulation of blood to the brain and to other changes happening in the body, the person may become restless or agitated.</li>
<li>To have a calming effect, speak in a quiet natural way, lightly massage the persons hand or forehead, or softly play familiar music.</li>
<li>Medications can be given to the patient.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-of-death">SIGNS OF DEATH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-of-death" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Breathing stops</li>
<li>No heartbeat or pulse can be felt</li>
<li>The person cannot be woken up</li>
<li>Eyelids may be half open</li>
<li>Sometimes their mouth may also be open</li>
<li>Pupils are fixed</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bereavement-and-grief">BEREAVEMENT AND GRIEF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bereavement-and-grief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Bereavement</strong>  is the loss of something of value (not only of a person could be loss of jobs)
or</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is the situation of anyone who has lost a person who they are attached to.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Grief</strong>  is a persons reaction to loss and includes a range of emotions on the psychosocial, social, spiritual, physical and emotional reaction to loss.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY OMS</p>
<ul>
<li>Mourning  refers to the behavior and actions of someone who is bereaved, it includes traditional customs and practices around death</li>
<li>Is the process of adaptations, including the cultural and social rituals prescribed as accompaniments.</li>
<li>Loss  signifies absence of an object, position, ability or attribute. Often applied to the death of an individual, and it is the bereaved who is considered to be experiencing a loss.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY OHSAS 18001:2015</p>
<ul>
<li>Different sorts of loss</li>
<li>Loss of face, security, retirement, marriage, divorce, income and death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="grief">GRIEF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#grief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Grief begins before the death of the patient and the survivor may anticipate and experience loss</li>
<li>It includes a series of stages or tasks that the survivor moves through to resolve grief. No one really gets over a loss, but can heal and learn to live with the loss</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY OMS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-griefs">TYPES OF GRIEFS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-griefs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Anticipatory</strong>  this is grief before loss associated with diagnosis, acute and chronic illness and terminal illness experienced by the patients, family and care giver</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Normal grief</strong>  this is normally exhibited by normal psychological response / feelings characterized by anger, numbness, disbelief, depression and disappear along with physical symptoms example  fatigue, poor sleep etc.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li><strong>Anger</strong>  this is the pain of separation; -</li>
<li>searching for a person</li>
<li>anxiety, burden of guilt or anger for the survivor of a partners death and their non impending death leaving children orphans.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY OHSAS 18001:2015</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Numbness</strong>  this is a protective mechanism which lasts from a hours to a week but should not extend beyond this point.</li>
<li><strong>Disbelief</strong>  lasts for weeks or months presuming that the deceased has only gone away.</li>
<li>When this is over the person opens up to grieving process.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY OMS-3000</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Types of abnormal grief</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Delayed  this is defined by an absence of grieving within the 1st weeks or months after death. It is often precipitated many years later by further loss. It is more likely to be more severe and chronic when it finally occurs. Help the client accepted reality of the past life.</li>
<li>Inhibited grief  occurs when all the reminders of the bereaved depression.</li>
<li>this mechanism of avoidance may work for some but can present as irritability, restlessness and depression.</li>
<li>Guided mourning is employed to encourage the bereaved to face reality of the loss.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Chronic grief</strong>  may be severe and occurs when a person fails to progress through all the tasks of mourning. There is no fixed time period. Assist the bereaved to move on in the grieving process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Persistent hypochondriasis</strong>  this may occur and block grief. The bereaved takes on the symptom of the deceased or developed symptoms related to anxiety or depression. Explain to the patient what is happening, maybe all that is required. However note that the mortality and mobility of widows and widowers is increased in the first year after death due to the depression.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<ul>
<li>Psychiatric disorder  severe depressive illness may develop with delusional ideas of guilt and suicidal intent. May require hospitalization.</li>
<li>Mania, phobic disorders, alcoholism and drug addiction may occur.</li>
<li>Risk factors that complicate the grief.</li>
<li>Sudden or trauma death</li>
<li>Suicidal homicide</li>
<li>Death of a child</li>
<li>Multiple losses</li>
<li>Unpleasant death</li>
<li>Unpleasant death</li>
<li>Previously unresolved losses</li>
<li>Unresolved anger</li>
<li>Excessive use of denial preventing anticipator grieving</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-grief-wheel">THE GRIEF WHEEL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-grief-wheel" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Can be applied to any loss, whether its death, divorce, retirement or loss of health.</li>
<li>It shows that people need to go through four phases of coming to terms with the loss</li>
<li>There is no clear dividing lines between phases, each phase merging into the next with some movements backwards and forwards</li>
<li>The concept neither suggests any time scale for grieving process for each phase</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED BY OMS-3</p>
<ul>
<li>The wheel is shown as completed at a higher level than it began because many people report through the process of adjusting to a loss, they have in some way, grown and become stronger.</li>
<li>However people will always react differently.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phases-of-grief">PHASES OF GRIEF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phases-of-grief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="initial-shock">INITIAL SHOCK<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#initial-shock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Numbness and disbelief before emotional reality of the loss is felt</li>
<li>Seeing the body, attending the funeral or visiting the grave are important in facilitating acceptance of the reality of death</li>
<li>Shock can be presented with; numbness and lack of feelings, probably due to acknowledging all the feelings would be overwhelming, disbelief and rejection</li>
<li>uncontrolled emotional excitement, thinking slow, chaotic or can remain unaffected, activity  slow super driver, or remain unaffected</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-pain-of-separation">THE PAIN OF SEPARATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-pain-of-separation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This affects the behavior and emotions</li>
<li>Bereaved suffer overwhelming periods of sickness as they are faced with everyday reality of their loss</li>
<li>They may try to reduce this by avoiding reminders of the deceased</li>
<li>They may also find themselves searching for the deceased, dreaming of them or even actually seeing them</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<ul>
<li>Visual or auditory hallucination at this time are normal, agitation, restlessness and inability to concentrate</li>
<li>Other emotions other than sadness may be experienced...i.e anxiety due to loss of the familiar routine and feelings of insecurity</li>
<li>Anger may be directed towards the deceased for abandoning them, towards God or towards professionals.</li>
<li>Guilt may occur when anger is directed internally.</li>
<li>Physical symptoms related autonomic nervous system e.g palpitation, insomnia, diarrhea and fatigue is experienced if transient hypochondriasis can occur.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acceptance-the-final-phase-resolution-and-re-organization">ACCEPTANCE; THE FINAL PHASE RESOLUTION AND RE ORGANIZATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acceptance-the-final-phase-resolution-and-re-organization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Eventually loss is accepted and life without the deceased is adjusted</li>
<li>Emotional energy is re-invested in new relationships and activities although anniversaries often trigger renewed grief</li>
<li>Developing balanced memorial, realistic memory of the deceased, both good and bad aspects of their personalities</li>
<li>Control over remembering some choice over when and what to remember, no longer pre-occupied with memories</li>
<li>Return to previous levels of functioning. A resumption of activities, interests, motivation and abilities.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Changed values. A different view of the relative importance of or things new insight.</li>
<li>New meaning in life. A new sense of purpose.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-bereavement-and-grief">MANAGEMENT OF BEREAVEMENT AND GRIEF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-bereavement-and-grief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ways-of-helping-the-bereaved">WAYS OF HELPING THE BEREAVED<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ways-of-helping-the-bereaved" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Being there</li>
<li>By listening in an accepting, non-judgmental way</li>
<li>By tolerating silences</li>
<li>By showing that you are listening and that you understand</li>
<li>By encouraging them to talk about the deceased</li>
<li>By being familiar with your own feelings about loss and grief</li>
<li>By offering reassurance</li>
<li>By not taking anger personally</li>
<li>By recognizing that your feelings may reflect how they feel</li>
<li>By accepting that you cannot make them feel better</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="last-offices-care-of-the-dead-body">LAST OFFICES (CARE OF THE DEAD BODY)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#last-offices-care-of-the-dead-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Remove all things  money, bangles, rings, necklaces, earrings, artificial dentives. Put them in a container and label and put them in a safe place to be given to a close family member.</li>
<li>Wedding ring not removed, strap it and record in the cordex</li>
<li>Remove the pillows, I.V fluids, blood transfusion, strengthen the legs and put them together. Close the eyes and the mouth. If the mouth isnt closing use strapping</li>
<li>Clean the body and remove all the soiled linen and cover the body with clean linen</li>
<li>Arrange hair smartly and leave it to lie flat</li>
<li>After 1hr prepare to take the body to the mortuary.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">PROCEDURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Equipment required</li>
<li>Mortuary sheet</li>
<li>Soap and bowl with warm water</li>
<li>Towel</li>
<li>Brush and comb</li>
<li>Container for soiled dressing</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">PROCEDURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Clean the body rinse and dry</li>
<li>Cut the nails and clean</li>
<li>Any dressing if clean leave it, if dirty change</li>
<li>Close all the orifices..i.e the ears, the nose and the vagina to stop any discharge that may ooze out.</li>
<li>Put lower limbs together.</li>
<li>Arms put in either sides and tie the body</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-death-and-grief">STAGES OF DEATH AND GRIEF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-death-and-grief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anytime we suffer a significant loss, we experience grief</li>
<li>The intensity of the grief depends on the loss</li>
<li>The loss could be the end of a meaningful relationship, the breakup of ones family, the death of a pet, the death of a family member.</li>
</ul>
<p>Elisabeth Kubler-Ross</p>
<p>.</p>
<p>Stage 2; ANGER</p>
<ul>
<li>Anger may be displaced and projected in the environment, the hostility may be directed towards family members, friends and always directed to the staff</li>
<li>Patients feel quite relieved after expelling the anger</li>
<li>The nurse should tolerate and not feel offended and not abuse the patient back</li>
<li>They should give the patient time and not neglect them</li>
<li>Help them when they are okay s much as possible</li>
<li>Address anger directed towards other patients and visitors.</li>
</ul>
<p>Stage 3; BARGAINING</p>
<ul>
<li>Patients try to extend the eventuality and seek to postpone death by making promises to God mostly</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<p>Stage 4; DEPRESSION</p>
<ul>
<li>Patient becomes depressed and starts preparing for the loss of everyone and everything she likes.</li>
<li>Patients grieve as they prepare for final separation</li>
<li>They feel sadness and often cries as though mourning for their own death</li>
<li>They become very withdrawn and wants to be left alone and at times cover themselves with a blanket or sheet</li>
<li>May refuse medication.</li>
<li>The nurse should stay with the patient and listen to them but not comment.</li>
<li>Be there and provide moral support</li>
<li>Dont disturb the patients when they want to be alone.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED BY</p>
<p>Stage 5; ACCEPTANCE.</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient finally accepts death. This stage is peaceful and calm.</li>
<li>Some thank the Lord because of the years they have lived, while some are peaceful because of living their families settled</li>
<li>Patient is neither depressed nor angry, and kind accepts whats going to happen.</li>
<li>His interests may diminish, no feelings, patients may sleep and rest and desires no news nor vision</li>
<li>Some write wills, some call their children for advice, sharing property and bless them</li>
<li>the nurses should at least tenderly touch the patient and reassure them.</li>
<li>Continue with support and assists where necessary like calling for a relative when they ask.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
K</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="arguments-for-or-against-surgery">ARGUMENTS FOR OR AGAINST SURGERY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arguments-for-or-against-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arguments-against-surgery">Arguments against surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arguments-against-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Survival is driven by the rate and volume metastatic burden</li>
<li>Unhealthy patients that can't tolerate surgery</li>
<li>Risk benefit ratio is heavily weighted towards the risks.</li>
<li>Theoretical risk of angering the tumor or letting the air in.</li>
<li>Advanced /incurable disease a curse</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>
<p>Arguments for surgery</p>
<ul>
<li>Improving quality of life and symptoms control</li>
<li>Debulking gives chemotherapy a fighting chance</li>
<li>After the metastatic cascade</li>
<li>Remove the primary tumor</li>
<li>Removing the metastases</li>
<li>Removing the inhibitory peptides /molecules that depress the local immune response to the tumor enhancing the anti-tumor immunity to the remaining cells</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="roles-of-surgery-in-pc">Roles of surgery in PC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#roles-of-surgery-in-pc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li><strong>Initial evaluation of the disease</strong></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>ranges from minor procedures such as biopsy of suspicious lumps and / or lymph nodes to more invasive procedures like cystoscopy or endoscopy. This helps in diagnosis making</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li><strong>Local disease control</strong></li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>debulking aimed at decreasing tumor size such as intra-abdominal malignancies (ovarian and nephroblastoma.)</li>
<li>Control of fungating lesions to achieve symptom control especially in breast cancer or in peripheral lesions such as kaposis sarcoma, head and neck.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Control of hemorrhage</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>commonest among vesico-vaginal or recto-vaginal fistula as complication of cancer of the cervix. (direct result or due to radio therapy)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Pain control</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Relief of obstruction from dysphagia in head, neck and esophageal cancer</li>
<li>Insertion of gastrostomy and stents</li>
<li>Relief of intestinal obstruction following ovarian, rectal and colon cancer</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Reconstruction and rehabilitation</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>not common in poor resource settings but useful in improving quality of life for patients with breast, head and neck cancer</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="palliattive-chemotherapy">PALLIATTIVE CHEMOTHERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palliattive-chemotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to use of drugs to stop or to kill the growth of cancer cells.</li>
<li>Given orally, intravenously, or into the peritoneal or pleural cavity</li>
<li>Forms a specialized area of cancer care and treatment for radical cure (burkitts lymphoma)</li>
<li>The palliative/toxicity trade off from treatment clearly favors symptom relief.</li>
<li>Chemotherapy was once regarded as an often futile and always dangerous kind of therapy by both the public and many palliative physician and nurses</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<ul>
<li>Duration of chemotherapy</li>
<li>A chemotherapy cycle consists of the days the drugs are administered followed by a rest and the recovery period.</li>
<li>A cycle usually lasts from one to four weeks and is then repeated, thus the treatment is administered for one to four weeks.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED SYSTEM</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="radiotherapy">RADIOTHERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Radiation onchology</strong>  is a medical specialist that involves controlled use of radiation to treat cancer either for cure, or to reduce pain and other symptoms caused by cancer.</li>
<li>Radiotherapy is a cancer treatment that uses high doses of radiation to kill cancer cells and shrink tumors.</li>
<li><strong>Uses of radiotherapy</strong></li>
<li>curative</li>
<li>palliative</li>
<li>control of growth of recurring non-cancer growth</li>
<li><strong>types of radiation</strong></li>
<li>external beam</li>
<li>internal i.e brachytherapy</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
CERTIFIED</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="duration-of-treatment">duration of treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#duration-of-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Each session is quick and painless lasting about 15 minutes. Typically people have treatment sessions 5 times per week.</p>
<p>The schedule continues 3-9 weeks targeting only the tumor.</p>
<ul>
<li>Procedure</li>
<li>External radiotherapy  where a machine directs beams of radiation at the cancer</li>
<li>A radioactive implant inside your body near the cancer</li>
<li>A radioactive liquid that you swallow or injected</li>
<li>Directly at the tumor during surgery (intrabeam radiotherapy)</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>CERTIFIED</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pain-relief">Pain relief<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pain-relief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Metastatic bone pain</li>
<li>Painful lymphadenopathy</li>
<li>Pain due to soft tissue infiltration by cancer</li>

<ul>
<li>Although hormones do not usually affect cancer cells, oestrogen and progesterone affect the growth of some breast cancer, while testosterone affect the growth of some prostrate cancer. This means drugs that block the effects or lower the levels of these hormones can be used to treat some types of breast and prostrate cancer.</li>
</ul>
